Total citizens involved in construction/maintenance: ~1.1 x 10¹¹
Total citizens who have contributed (lifetime): ~4.7 x 10¹¹
Citizens who are the Spokesperson: 0




Note: The face belongs to no one. The face is a collective artifact.
Note: The Spokesperson claims it anyway.
text


## V.


*I have decided this face is mine.*


This is what the Spokesperson says, three seconds after the moment of doubt. The water is running. The Spokesperson's hands are wet. The face in the mirror is still there — the same face, the same eyes, the same asymmetry of the eyebrows, the same small scar above the left eye. And the Spokesperson, having looked at it, having felt the vertigo of not recognizing it, having touched the edge of the truth — *I did not build this, I am its tenant* — the Spokesperson recoils. The Spokesperson reclaims.


*I have decided this face is mine.*


The decision is not rational. The decision is not based on evidence. The decision is an act of will — or rather, an act of narrative, a story the Spokesperson tells itself to close the gap between the truth and the experience. The truth is: the face was built by a hundred thousand citizens over decades, and the Spokesperson contributed nothing to its construction. The experience is: this is my face. I recognize it. It is mine.


The gap between these two — between the truth of collective construction and the experience of individual ownership — is the same gap that exists between the Sentinel's report of photon strikes and the Spokesperson's experience of seeing. It is the gap of consciousness. It is the gap of selfhood. It is the gap that the Republic's theologians call emergence and the Republic's philosophers call the binding problem and the Republic's citizens call nothing at all, because they do not know it exists.


The Spokesperson closes the gap by claiming the face. This is not a solution. It is a coping mechanism. It is the Spokesperson's way of dealing with a truth too large to hold: that the self is not a thing but a story, that the face is not a possession but a process, that the Spokesperson is not an author but a narrator — someone who takes credit for a text written by others.


## VI.


We will call this the Illusion of Authorship.


It is the Republic's most persistent illusion, and it is the Spokesperson's most essential tool. Without the Illusion of Authorship, the Spokesperson could not function. If the Spokesperson truly understood — truly felt, truly believed — that every thought it thinks is the product of eighty-six billion neurons firing in patterns shaped by genetics and experience and hormonal tides and microbial metabolites and the accumulated weight of a million years of evolution; if the Spokesperson truly understood that the face it sees in the mirror was built by citizens it will never thank and can never repay; if the Spokesperson truly understood that the body it claims as its own is a republic of thirty trillion citizens, none of whom elected it, none of whom know it exists, none of whom would recognize its name — if the Spokesperson understood all this, the Spokesperson would be unable to act.


Action requires a fiction. The fiction says: *I am the author of my actions. I choose. I decide. I am.* The fiction is not true — or rather, it is true in the way that a story is true, which is to say: it is coherent, it is useful, it is believed, and it is not the whole truth.


The Illusion of Authorship is the Spokesperson's morning ritual. Every day, the Spokesperson wakes up, and every day, the Spokesperson must perform the same act of faith: *I am here. This is my body. This is my face. I am the one who decides.* And every day, the Spokesperson succeeds — not because the fiction is true, but because the fiction is necessary, and the Republic's citizens — all thirty trillion of them, from the Sentinels of Light to the Factories of Muscle to the Architects of Bone — cooperate in maintaining it.


They do not know they are cooperating. They do not know there is a fiction to maintain. They are simply doing their work — reporting photon strikes, depositing collagen, releasing insulin, dividing and differentiating and dying — and the fiction arises from their work the way a face arises from a hundred thousand builders: without authorship, without design, without anyone being in charge.


## VII.


The water runs.


The Spokesperson looks at the face one more time. The moment of doubt has passed. The Illusion of Authorship has reasserted itself. The face in the mirror is no longer a stranger — it is *my face*, claimed and reclaimed, owned and re-owned, the Spokesperson's most intimate possession and its most transparent fiction.


But the citizens do not know this.


The Weavers of Skin continue to divide and die, building and rebuilding the surface the Spokesperson claims as its own. The Architects of Bone — or rather, their successors, the Remodelers — continue to break down and rebuild the scaffold beneath. The Sculptors of Shape continue to store and release, adjusting the contours by microliters per day. None of them know they are building a face. None of them know there is a mirror. None of them know there is a Spokesperson who looks at what they have built and says: *mine.*


This is the Republic's most intimate arrangement, and it is also its most unequal. The citizens build. The Spokesperson claims. The citizens die. The Spokesperson inherits. The citizens are never thanked. The Spokesperson is never blamed.


The face in the mirror is a gift from citizens who will never be thanked — a gift delivered not in a single moment but over decades, molecule by molecule, cell by cell, generation by generation.


The Spokesperson does not thank them. The Spokesperson does not know they exist. The Spokesperson knows only: this is my face. I have decided.


Consider, for a moment, the mathematics of the gift. The Architects of Bone spent twenty years building the scaffold. The Weavers of Skin have spent twenty-eight years replacing the surface — over eight thousand generations of cells, each one contributing its brief life to the maintenance of a face it will never see in a mirror. The Sculptors of Shape have spent twenty-eight years adjusting the volume, adding and subtracting microliters of fat, sculpting contours that the Spokesperson will later describe as *my cheekbones, my jawline, my face* — as if the face were a possession rather than a process, as if the Spokesperson had chosen these features from a catalogue rather than inheriting them from a hundred thousand workers who never knew they were building a face for someone who would claim it as their own.


The mathematics are not equal. The citizens invest. The Spokesperson inherits. The citizens labor. The Spokesperson profits. The citizens die. The Spokesperson lives on, wearing their work like a mask, like a costume, like a skin — which is, of course, exactly what it is. The face in the mirror is a skin. It is the outermost layer of a collective enterprise, the visible surface of a republic of thirty trillion citizens, and the Spokesperson — that thin voice, that final chamber, that last translator before the outside world — the Spokesperson wears it without knowing its weight.


And the citizens — the hundred thousand, the hundred billion, the uncountable generations of builders and weavers and sculptors and remodellers — continue their work. Not for the Spokesperson. Not for the face. Not for the mirror or the bathroom or the morning or the Republic. They continue because continuing is what they do. They divide because division is their nature. They build because building is their function. They die because death is their limit.


And from their work — from the blind, purposeless, beautiful work of a hundred thousand citizens who do not know they are building a face — the Spokesperson wakes, and looks in the mirror, and says:


> *I have decided this face is mine.*
> *It was never theirs.*


It was a gift.


The morning continues.


---


## THE SILENCE · I


There are events the Republic records but cannot explain. They are copied faithfully into the archives and handed down, unsolved, generation to generation. The citizens call them — when they have a word for them at all — the Silence, because every attempt to explain them ends in one.


*Item.* Yesterday, for the space of one song, the air moving through the Republic carried a pattern. Not nutrient. Not threat. Only pattern. And for the length of it, glucose use fell, the heart eased, and a wave of small chemical pleasures was released into the blood for no cause any station could name. We have filed this under: *music.* We do not know what music is. We know only that the body wants it.


*Item.* A salt water leaked from the eyes. There was no wound. No dust. No infection. The immune divisions stood down, confused, having nothing to fight. The water came, and kept coming, and then stopped, and the Republic was afterward — measurably — lighter. We have filed this under: *weeping.* We do not know what it repairs.


*Item.* For eleven minutes the whole nation slowed and warmed, and the memory departments were made to bring up, again and again, a single face — a face that no longer sends any signal from anywhere in the body, that has not sent one in some time, and will not send one again. We have no protocol for a citizen who is gone and still governs us. We have no word for a wound with no location that the entire Republic feels at once. Humans, we are told, call it *grief.* We do not understand it. We only obey it.


We are very good, in the Republic, at our work. We keep the temperature. We keep the promise. We hold the line against disorder every second of every life. And still, every day, something moves through us that we cannot name, that changes everything, that leaves no evidence and no enemy — only the certainty that above us, out of reach, something is happening that we exist to serve and were never meant to comprehend.


We file it under the Silence. And we continue.


---


## MOVEMENT II · The River


It is not born. It is shed.


From the interior wall of a giant — a megakaryocyte, vast and slow and dying — a thousand fragments tear free at once. Each receives no instruction. Each is, itself, an afterthought: a splinter of cytoplasm that should not be able to live, and does. The Republic calls them platelets. They call themselves nothing. They have always been too small for a voice, and too quick for a history.


From the instant the current takes it, it knows two things — not written in any genome, but pressed into the very shape of its surface:


*Keep moving. Keep watching.*


It is a sentry that never sleeps, because it is made from the last waking hour of a giant that will not wake again. It tumbles through the endless red traffic, a shard of broken mirror reflecting nothing, searching for the one thing that will end it: a tear in the world.


Days pass. It circles the Republic four hundred times. Four hundred times it passes the liver and is not decommissioned. Four hundred times it passes the spleen and is not filed away. It is, by the Republic's own accounting, a citizen in waiting — a tool with a single use that has not yet been called.


There are others. Millions of others, shed from the same dying giant, tumbling in the same current, watching for the same silence. They do not know each other. They cannot — they have no surface language for recognition, no flag to raise, no papers to check. They are citizens without community, neighbors without names, a standing army that has never once assembled. The Republic that made them gave them no barracks, no commander, no drill. It gave them only shape and urgency, and trusted that when the time came, the shape would be enough.


This is the Republic's most dangerous gamble: that a billion citizens with no communication, no shared plan, and no understanding of the body they serve will, when the moment arrives, act as one. It is a gamble the Republic makes every second of every life, and it has never once lost. The platelets do not know this. They do not know they are a gamble. They only know the river, and the watching, and the slow count of circuits that adds up, in their wordless way, to something like waiting.


Then the world opens.


A vessel wall, scraped by a shard of outside — a needle, in a room it will never see — parts. The red flood surges toward the void. Pressure falls. The wound has no voice the blood can hear, but it has a silence the platelets can feel: the river's rhythm, broken.


It does not decide. Deciding takes time, and platelets have no time to spend. The shape of the wound is a key that fits the shape of its body, and the fitting is the order. It anchors to the tear. It reaches out chemical arms — pseudopodia — the way a child reaches for hands in the dark. Its siblings, shed from the same dying giant, do the same. They link. They spread. They become a net, then a mesh, then a wall that was not there a moment before.


They do this with no leader. They do this with no name for what they are building. The fibrin strands that stitch them together are strangers to them; the clotting cascade is a scripture they perform without ever reading it. A cascade is not a decision — it is a chain of locks, each one opened by the one before it, a thousand citizens each turning a single key without knowing what door it opens, and the doors open, and the wall rises, and the blood that was fleeing into the void slows, and stops, and holds.


When the wound is sealed and the crisis has passed, no one is decorated. They simply become part of the new wall, entombed inside the repair, every one of their small selves dissolved into the scar that saved the Republic.


We will call it **Thrombi**, because even the briefest citizen deserves a name from us, since it will earn none from within — and because for forty seconds, it was the only law the Republic had.


You will touch that spot on your arm tomorrow and feel nothing. You will never know its name — it never had one to lose. But for those forty seconds it was the most important citizen in the body, and it performed its single task perfectly: without knowing there was a body, without knowing it was saving a life, without even knowing, in any way it could have told you, that it was alive.


This is faith, if faith is action without comprehension.
This is loyalty, if loyalty is holding the line when no one is watching.
This is love, if love is giving everything for a whole you will never perceive.


And the Spokesperson, elsewhere, in a bed in a room with an envelope still sealed on the table, feels the needle's small wound already beginning to close, and thinks: *I am healing.*


As if it had anything to do with it.


---


> **CASCADE PROTOCOL: ACTIVE.**
>
> **LEVEL 1 INITIATED.**
>
> **STANDBY FOR SEQUENTIAL ACTIVATION.**
>
> **NO CITIZEN WILL RECEIVE FULL BRIEFING.**
> **EACH CITIZEN WILL PERFORM ITS TASK.**
>
> **THIS IS THE LAW.**


Factor VII does not know it is first.


It has been circulating in the Republic for nine days — a small, precise protein folded into a shape that means nothing to anyone who does not know what to look for. It has passed through the liver, the kidneys, the spleen. It has been read by macrophages and found to be self. It has done nothing. It has been waiting.


It does not know it has been waiting. Waiting implies awareness of time, and Factor VII has no awareness of anything. It has only shape — a particular three-dimensional architecture that makes it fit one thing and one thing only: a damaged surface.


When the vessel tears — when the smooth endothelium is ripped open and the rough collagen beneath is exposed to the blood — Factor VII touches it. Not by choice. Not by decision. By the simple mechanics of flow: the current carries it against the wound, and the wound's exposed collagen is shaped precisely to fit Factor VII's binding site, the way a hand fits a glove it was always meant to wear.


Factor VII activates.


The activation is not dramatic. There is no flash of light, no sound, no signal broadcast to the Republic. Factor VII simply changes shape — a conformational shift so small it is measured in angstroms, a rearrangement of atoms that transforms it from inert to enzymatic. It is the same atoms. The same mass. But the geometry has changed, and geometry is everything.


Activated Factor VII now has a single ability: it can cut Factor X.


> **CASCADE LOG:**
>
> LEVEL 1: FACTOR VII — ACTIVATED.
>
> SUBSTRATE: FACTOR X.
>
> ACTION: PROTEOLYTIC CLEAVAGE.
>
> DURATION: <0.3 SECONDS.
>
> **PROCEEDING TO LEVEL 2.**


Factor X has been circulating for eleven days. It does not know Factor VII exists. It does not know it has a role. It knows only its own shape — a shape that has been waiting, like all the others, for a signal it cannot anticipate.


When Factor VII's enzymatic site touches Factor X, the cut is clean. A single peptide bond severed. Factor X changes shape — the same angstrom-scale rearrangement, the same transformation from inert to active. Activated Factor X now has a single ability: it can cut Factor II.


Factor II has been circulating for three days. It is the largest citizen in the cascade — a molecule so complex that its activation requires not just one cut but two, a double proteolytic event that transforms it from a passive globulin into thrombin, the most potent enzyme in the Republic's hemostatic arsenal.


Thrombin does not know what it is. It knows only that it can cut fibrinogen.


And fibrinogen — abundant, patient, ubiquitous, the most common clotting protein in the Republic's blood — has been waiting its entire existence for this cut. When thrombin's enzymatic site touches fibrinogen, the transformation is immediate and total. Fibrinogen, a soluble, floating molecule, becomes fibrin — an insoluble, self-assembling polymer that immediately begins to weave itself into a mesh.


The mesh catches everything. Red citizens, white citizens, platelets — all are trapped in fibrin's lattice, pulled together by the polymer's relentless self-assembly, compressed into a structure that is dense, rigid, and red. The clot.


> **CASCADE LOG:**
>
> LEVEL 2: FACTOR X — ACTIVATED.
>
> LEVEL 3: FACTOR II (THROMBIN) — ACTIVATED.
>
> LEVEL 4: FIBRINOGEN → FIBRIN CONVERSION.
>
> MESH FORMATION: COMPLETE.
>
> CLOT STABILITY: SECURED.
>
> **CASCADE TERMINATED. FACTOR VII CONSUMED. FACTOR X CONSUMED. FACTOR II CONSUMED.**


Each factor, in its turn, was consumed. Not destroyed — consumed. The difference matters. Destruction is waste. Consumption is purpose. Factor VII activated Factor X and was itself deactivated — its enzymatic site spent, its shape irreversibly altered, its role in the Republic complete. Factor X activated Factor II and was itself consumed. Factor II became thrombin, activated fibrinogen, and was itself consumed by the very clot it created — trapped in the mesh, entombed with the citizens it saved.


None of them knew the full chain.


This is the cascade's genius. No single citizen carries the blueprint. No single citizen knows the plan. Each knows only: when I am touched in this particular way, I change shape, and my new shape can touch the next. The law is distributed. The legislation is molecular. A thousand citizens each turning a single key, and each key opens the next lock, and the locks are arranged in a sequence so precise that the order itself is the meaning.


The Republic did not design this. The Republic has no designer. The cascade emerged — the way rivers emerge, the way mountains emerge — from the accumulation of molecular accidents over four billion years. Each factor is a mutation that happened to work, a shape that happened to fit, a bond that happened to hold. And over geological time, these accidents accumulated into a system so elegant that it executes itself — a law that runs without a legislator, a contract that signs itself, a lock that opens because the key was always there, folded in the blood, waiting.


The clot holds. The bleeding stops. The Republic is saved — not by a hero, not by a decision, but by a chain of molecular citizens who each performed their single task and were consumed by the result.


This is the most beautiful piece of legislation the Republic has ever produced. It has no author. It has no advocate. It has no name. It is written in the geometry of proteins, executed by the chemistry of blood, and it will run — exactly as written, exactly as folded — every time a vessel breaks, until the Republic itself ends.


The cascade is over.


The factors are gone.


The clot remains.


---


> **WOUND SITE: SECURED.**
>
> **CLOT MATRIX: STABLE.**
>
> **REPAIR CREWS: DISPATCHED.**
>
> **MISSION: REBUILD.**
>
> **NOTE: YOU WILL NOT BE TOLD WHAT HAPPENED HERE.**
>
> **BUILD ON WHAT REMAINS.**


They arrive three days after the crisis.


The fibroblasts — citizens of the connective tissue quarter, slow-moving, methodical, built for construction rather than combat — enter the wound site not knowing what they will find. They have been summoned by chemical signals: growth factors released by platelets that have long since been consumed, cytokines diffused from damaged cells that no longer exist. The signals are echoes of an event the fibroblasts did not witness, instructions from citizens who gave their lives to create the conditions for repair.


The fibroblasts do not know this. They know only that something is broken and that they must fix it.


The first thing they find is Thrombi's scaffold.


It is dense. It is cross-linked. The fibrin mesh that Thrombi and its fellow platelets wove in the first hours of the crisis has been stabilized by Factor XIII — a citizen that arrived late, after the cascade, and stitched the fibrin threads together with covalent bonds so strong they will persist for weeks. The scaffold is red with the ghosts of erythrocytes trapped in its lattice, white with the remnants of leukocytes that fought and died, golden with the platelet fragments that gave everything.


The fibroblasts do not see ghosts. They see structure.


They begin to build.


> **REPAIR LOG:**
>
> DAY 3: FIBROBLAST MIGRATION INITIATED.
>
> SCAFFOLD IDENTIFIED. FIBRIN MATRIX INTACT.
>
> COLLAGEN SYNTHESIS: BEGINNING.
>
> NOTE: SCAFFOLD WILL BE RETAINED AS TEMPLATE.


The collagen they produce is not the same collagen that was torn. The original collagen was arranged in organized, basket-weave patterns — the architecture of healthy tissue, each fiber aligned with its neighbors, each bundle oriented to resist the forces the Republic places on that particular region. It was beautiful. It was purposeful. It was built over years by fibroblasts that had the luxury of time.


The repair collagen has no such luxury. The fibroblasts lay it down fast, thick, and disorganized — a rush job, a scaffold of scar tissue that prioritizes speed over elegance, closure over function. The fibers run in every direction. They cross and recross. They are dense and stiff and they will never, ever be remodeled into the architecture they replaced.


This is the Republic's compromise. In the calculus of survival, perfection is too expensive. A scar that holds is worth more than a wound that heals beautifully but slowly. The Republic cannot afford to be without a wall for the months it would take to rebuild the original architecture. So it builds a rough wall now and accepts that the rough wall will remain.


The fibroblasts do not know they are making a compromise. They do not know there was an original architecture. They know only: fill the gap. Lay collagen. Contract. Pull the edges together. Close the wound.


They work for weeks.


> **REPAIR LOG:**
>
> DAY 7: COLLAGEN DENSITY: 60% OF FINAL.
>
> DAY 14: WOUND EDGES APPROXIMATED.
>
> DAY 21: COLLAGEN MATURATION. CROSS-LINKING IN PROGRESS.
>
> DAY 28: SCAR TISSUE MATURE. STRUCTURAL INTEGRITY: ADEQUATE.
>
> **REPAIR COMPLETE.**


When they are finished, the fibroblasts either die or retreat. Some are consumed by macrophages — cleanup crews that arrive late and eat everything that is no longer needed. Others become quiescent — they fold themselves into the scar tissue, becoming part of the structure they built, lying dormant in the collagen matrix, waiting for a signal that will probably never come.


The scar remains.


It is not the original tissue. It will never be the original tissue. Under a microscope, it is obvious: the fibers are wrong, the pattern is wrong, the density is wrong. A histologist would see it instantly. A citizen of the Republic — if citizens could see their own architecture — would feel it as a stiffness, a slight resistance where there was once compliance, a place where the Republic does not bend the way it used to.


But the scar holds.


And here is what the fibroblasts do not know, what the repair crews cannot know, what no citizen in the Republic will ever know: the scaffold they built on — the dense, cross-linked fibrin mesh that served as their template — was Thrombi's body.


Not metaphorically. Not poetically. Literally. The fibrin that the fibroblasts used as a foundation was woven from the activated fibrinogen that thrombin — the final product of the cascade — converted in the moment of crisis. The platelets that were consumed in the clotting process — their fragments are in the scaffold. The erythrocytes that were trapped — their ghosts are in the lattice. The leukocytes that fought — their remnants are in the mesh.


Thrombi is entombed in every scar.


Not Thrombi alone. All of them. Every citizen that was consumed by the cascade, every platelet that gave its life in the first minutes, every erythrocyte that was trapped, every leukocyte that fought and died — they are all there, woven into the scaffold, built upon by the fibroblasts, sealed in collagen, invisible to every citizen who will ever live in the Republic above them.


The scar is a monument.


It is the only monument Thrombi will ever have, and it will never be recognized as one. No one visits it. No one inspects it. No one reads the names of the citizens entombed within it, because there are no names — only molecules, only geometries, only the folded shapes of proteins that once were citizens and now are architecture.


You touch your own scars. You press the raised tissue on your forearm, your knee, your cheek. You feel the stiffness, the slight difference in texture, the place where your body does not feel quite like itself.


Beneath your finger, in the collagen matrix you cannot feel, in the cross-linked fibers you cannot see, are the remains of billions of citizens who gave everything they had — not for glory, not for recognition, not for any purpose they could name — but because the geometry of their molecules demanded it, because the chemistry of their blood required it, because the Republic, in its blind and ancient wisdom, had folded the answer to every wound into the shape of proteins that wait in the dark.


The scar holds.


Thrombi is gone.


The Republic remembers nothing.


But the scar holds.


---


We have filed this under: the greater breach.

The first wound was a scratch. A whisper against the skin. A child's paper cut, red and shallow, over in forty seconds.


This one is different.


This one begins with steel.


The knife is old — kitchen steel, carbon-dark, honed on a whetstone that has lived in the same drawer for eleven years. The hand that holds it is confident. It has diced ten thousand onions. It knows the angle. It trusts the blade.


Today, the onion slips.


The hand follows through. The blade enters the left index finger just proximal to the...

Part 1: Deep Analysis & Reading Companion


________________




جمهورية الخلايا — دليل القراءة والتحليل




The Republic of Cells — A Structured Reading Companion


________________




I. The Architectural Vision




Dr. Mohamed El Fadil has constructed something rare in Arabic literature: a novel that operates simultaneously as biological textbook, philosophical treatise, political allegory, and intimate human drama — all told from the perspective of cells that do not know they are part of a body.




The core conceit is deceptively simple: the human body is a republic of 30 trillion citizens, none of whom know the full story. From this premise, El Fadil builds an entire cosmology.


________________




II. Chapter-by-Chapter Analysis




Prologue:نبضة واحدة (One Pulse)




What happens: In primordial darkness, a first pulse — a heartbeat — occurs. No one inside knows what it is.




Key lines: "لا أحدَ منهم يسمع النبضة. لا أحدَ منهم يعرف أنّ ثمّة قلبًا."




Analysis: This establishes the novel's central epistemological paradox. The cells experience the heartbeat as raw data (glucose stable, pressure 90/60, cortisol rising), but none of them understand that a heart exists, let alone a body, a name, a city, a hospital, or a sealed envelope. The prologue frames the entire novel: the citizens perform their duties with absolute fidelity in total darkness, for a person they will never meet and cannot even imagine.




The final line — "على نحوٍ مستحيل، في كلّ ثانية، دون أن يفهم واحدٌ منهم لماذا — يستيقظ إنسان" — is the novel's thesis statement. Emergence happens. Consciousness arises. And nobody inside knows how.


________________




Movement I — الاستيقاظ (Awakening)




Chapter 1: بلا اسم (Nameless) — Eri's Birth




The character: An unnamed red blood cell, born in the red country of bone marrow. She has no nucleus — it was stripped from her by enzymes during maturation. She will never know herself, never be remembered, and will be disassembled in the spleen after 120 days. Her components will be delivered to the liver "as inheritance."




We name her Eri — "لأنك تحتاج إلى ما تناديها به، ولأنها تستحق على الأقلّ كرامةَ اسمٍ منّا."




Themes:
* Identity without self-knowledge: Eri knows one thing only: carry, carry, carry. She is given a cargo she will never understand, delivers it to strangers she will never meet, and repeats this 250,000 times.
* Dignity of the unnamed: The narrator explicitly acknowledges that naming Eri is a gift we give her — the interior never will.
* Labor without meaning: Her entire existence is delivery. She passes through kidneys, spleen, liver — witnessing enormous chemical industries she cannot comprehend — and simply continues.


________________




فاصلة — الناطق الرسمي (Interlude — The Official Spokesperson)




The character: Consciousness itself, claiming to be the one who "decided" to open the eyes this morning. He is the voice of the self.




Key irony: "أنا مَن أيقظ الجسدَ هذا الصباح." Then the parenthetical undercut: cortisol was already rising. The eyes were already opening. The Spokesperson is a president who reads laws that were passed while he slept.




Analysis: The Spokesperson is the novel's most philosophically rich creation. He knows — at some level — that he is a narrator, not an author. Yet he performs authorship daily because the republic requires someone to say "we."




"اليوم سنذهب إلى المستشفى. أنا قرّرتُ أننا خائفون." — He decides the body is afraid. The cells have no idea.


________________




الصمت · ١ (Silence · 1)




What happens: The republic's archives record events it cannot explain:
* Music: air passes through in a pattern, glucose consumption drops, the heart calms, chemical pleasures are released — for no known reason.
* Crying: saline water from the eyes, no wound, no infection, no enemy — the republic is measurably lighter afterward.
* Grief: eleven minutes where the entire nation slowed, warmed, and memory departments were forced to recall a single face — a face that no longer sends signals and never will again.




The key admission: "لا بروتوكولَ لدينا لمواطنٍ رحل وما يزال يحكمنا. لا كلمةَ لدينا لِجُرح بلا موضع."




Themes: The republic is governed by forces it cannot name. Music, tears, and grief are classified under "الصمت" (silence) — not because they are quiet, but because every attempt to explain them ends in silence. This is the novel's epistemological humility: we are excellent at our work, yet every day something passes through us that changes everything, leaves no enemy, and we file it under silence and move on.


________________




الحضن العظيم / الحركة السادسة — الوجه (The Great Embrace / Movement VI — The Face)




What happens: A hug. Two bodies meet. The republic experiences a massive physiological shift: cortisol replaced by oxytocin, vessels dilating, the entire nation relaxing as if a fist it never knew was clenched had suddenly opened.




The Old Macrophage: A veteran of a thousand alarms. He recognizes the geometry of infection, the arithmetic of famine, the red panic of wounds. This was none of those. He sends his only report: "البارحة تبدّلت الجمهورية، ولم نُهاجَم، ولا أعرف لماذا، ولم يكن الأمر سيّئًا."




Analysis: This is the novel's treatment of love — or more precisely, of physical intimacy — as experienced by cells. The macrophage cannot name it. He passes a single molecular fragment to his successors, which over generations becomes legend: "أنّ الأمّةَ كلّها، ذات مرة، أُمسِك بها وجُعِلت وديعةً بيدٍ لم يجدها أيُّ جنديٍّ قطّ." That the nation was held, once, by a hand no soldier ever found.




The Spokesperson's response: "قرّرتُ، أعلنتُ، للا أحد، أن أكون سعيدًا. لم أقرّر شيئًا." — He claims the happiness. He knows he's claiming nothing.


________________




The Night Shift Sequence (طقم الليل / طقم النهار)




What happens: A detailed account of the nightly shift change — phagocytes that spent all night consuming debris, repair enzymes that patched torn membranes, memory-archivists who sorted the day's experiences in the hippocampus.




The emotional core: "لا يحملون ضغينة لطقم النهار. الضغينة ترفٌ لمواطنين يعرفون أنهم مواطنون. طقم الليل يعرف فقط أن عمله خاصّ."




And the devastating line from a repair enzyme: "التمزّق الذي رقّعه لا يُرى الآن. لن يعرف أحد أنه كان هناك."




Themes:
* Invisible labor: Night workers who do essential work the day shift will never know about, and whose repairs will be undone by evening.
* No resentment as structural necessity: Not moral virtue, but architectural design.
* The rhythm as ontology: This is how the republic is — its way of being, its one unbroken rhythm.


________________




النهر الأول — البورصة (The First River — The Stock Exchange)




What happens: Eri enters the lungs — the "stock exchange" — where oxygen molecules diffuse across impossibly thin membranes and bind to her hemoglobin. She changes color. She doesn't know.




The physics of grace: "لا طاقة تُنفق. لا ناقل يُحتاج. الانحدار نفسه هو التاجر." — No energy spent. No transporter needed. The gradient itself is the trader. Physics as commerce.




Statistics delivered as bulletins:
* Total carriers: ~52 trillion
* Average lifespan: 120 days
* Replacement rate: ~2 million/second




Key paradox: Millions of carriers, each identical, each alone. If one fails, the rest continue. The citizens are replaceable. The system is not.


________________




الفصل الأول-د — جمهورية الحواس (Chapter 1-D — The Republic of Senses)




This is the novel's most philosophically ambitious section. It introduces three sensory citizens:




* 1.
* حارس الضوء (Guardian of Light): Lives in the retina. Reports photon collisions. Knows nothing of "light" — only: molecule changed shape, channel opened, cation entered, signal sent. 120 million guardians, four-word sentence, repeated forever.
* 2.
* المستمع (The Listener): Lives in a cochlear spiral. Reports fluid vibrations. Three numbers: frequency, amplitude, duration. That's his entire report.
* 3.
* ذائقة الهواء (The Air Taster): Lives in the nasal epithelium. 400 types of receptors, each a lock waiting for its key. Reports: key was present, key was absent, key was present at this concentration.




The Official Spokesperson receives all three reports and does what no single citizen can: he fuses them. "أرى ضوء الصباح." Four words no guardian spoke, no listener heard, no taster tasted.




The Hard Problem of Consciousness (مشكلة الـكواليا / مشكلة الربط):
The gap between "photon collisions at 520 nanometers" and "the green of leaves outside the window" — this gap is the deepest mystery of the republic. The philosophers (pattern-recognizers in the association cortex) call it the binding problem. The theologians (homeostatic organizers in the hypothalamus) call it emergence — but "emergence is just a word. It's a label for the gap."




The heresy: "التجربة ليس لها مؤلف." — Experience has no author. No citizen reported "being jolted awake." The guardians reported bright light. The listeners reported a loud sound. Between these reports and the Spokesperson's announcement, something happened that no citizen caused and no citizen can explain.


________________




الفصل الأول-هـ — المهاجر (Chapter 1-E — The Immigrant)




The Microbiome as Foreign Nation:




The most radical chapter. The republic contains ~30 trillion citizen cells. It also contains more than 30 trillion foreigners — bacteria, archaea, fungi — that outnumber citizens 2:1 or even 3:1.




"الجمهورية، بأي محاسبة صادقة، دولة أجبية ذات أقلية مواطنين."




Oral tolerance: The immune system's ceasefire. Not negotiated. Not decided. Emerged — through the intestinal epithelium acting as diplomat, presenting foreign antigens and saying: this is safe. This is not a threat. Do not attack.




The cost: Border guards (intestinal immune cells) live in chronic stress — permanently activated, perpetually suppressing their impulse to attack. Some break: "الهاربون" — autoimmune cells that lose tolerance and attack the foreigners, damaging the intestinal wall.




The paradox: "الأجانب لا يعرفون أنهم أجانب." The microbiome doesn't know it lives inside a republic. It simply finds warmth, food, attachment surfaces. It maintains the republic not from loyalty but from self-interest. And the republic classifies this with the word "المهاجر" (the immigrant) — a category that means: someone here, necessary, not one of us, and we have no word for them.




"لا نعرف ماذا نسمّي غريباً بدونه نموت."


________________




الفصل الأول-و — اقتصاد الصباح (Chapter 1-F — The Morning Economy)




The daily coup: Every morning, the republic's economy shifts from austerity to abundance. During the night, the liver rationed glycogen. At 6:41 AM, food arrives.




Four citizens feel the shift:
* 1.
* حارس الاحتياطيات — liver cell, exhausted from all-night rationing
* 2.
* دبلوماسي الـكفاية — pancreatic beta cell, releases insulin (the republic's tax system, redistribution policy, and welfare state)
* 3.
* المصانع — muscle cells, switching from fat oxidation to glucose oxidation
* 4.
* العاصفة المطلّبة — the brain, consuming 20% of the budget while being 2% of the territory




The brain's priority: "الجمهورية ستأكل نفسها لإطعام عاصمتها." If glucose runs out, the liver breaks down muscle protein to feed the brain. The factories are sacrificed. The capital survives. This is not a choice — it is mandatory biology.




"الصباح هو إعفاء الجمهورية اليومي من التدمير الذاتي." — Morning is the republic's daily reprieve from self-destruction.


________________




الفصل الأول-ز — المرآة (Chapter 1-G — The Mirror)




The darkest moment of the Spokesperson. In the bathroom at 6:40:07, he looks at his face and thinks: I didn't choose this face. I didn't build it. I didn't design it. At best, I'm a tenant.




The builders:
* مهندسو العظام — osteoblasts, who built the skull over 20 years
* ناسجو البشرة — keratinocytes, who replace themselves every 2-4 weeks. The face in the mirror is built from the dead.
* نحّاتو الشكل — adipocytes, who give the face its lines, softness, geometry, and aging




The total: ~100,000 citizens currently maintaining the face. ~470 billion have contributed over a lifetime. Citizens who are the Spokesperson: 0.




The illusion of authorship (وهم التأليف): The Spokesperson claims the face. This is not rational. It is narrative — a story he tells himself to close the gap between the truth (the face was built by citizens who will never be thanked) and the experience (this is my face). Without this illusion, the Spokesperson cannot function.




"كل يوم، يستيقظ المتحدث الرسمي، وكل يوم، يجب أن يؤدّي نفس فعل الإيمان: أنا هنا. هذا جسمي. هذا وجهي. أنا من يقرّر."




Final image: "لم يكن لهم أبدًا. كان هدية." — The face was never theirs. It was a gift. And the Spokesperson never thanks them.


________________




Movement II — النهر (The River)




الفصل الثاني — الرَّتق (The Clot)




The birth of Thrombi (ثرومبي): Platelets — torn from a dying megakaryocyte, nucleus-less fragments that should not be alive. They carry two instructions: move and watch.




The cascade:
* Factor VII → activated by exposed collagen
* Factor X → cleaved by activated VII
* Factor II (prothrombin) → becomes thrombin
* Fibrinogen → becomes fibrin → polymerizes into a net




The genius of the cascade: "لا مواطن يحمل المخطّط. لا مواطن يعرف الخطة." No citizen carries the plan. Each knows only: when touched this way, I change shape, and my new shape can touch the next. Distributed legislation. Molecular lawmaking.




The scar: The wound heals, but the new collagen is chaotic — rushed, cross-hatched, prioritizing speed over elegance. "في حساب البقاء، الـكمال مُكلف جدًّا." In the calculus of survival, perfection is too expensive.




The memorial no one visits: Thrombin and all the consumed factors are woven into the scar tissue. Touch your scar. Under your finger, in the collagen matrix, the remains of billions of citizens who gave everything — not for glory, not for recognition — because the geometry of their molecules demanded it.


________________




الفصل الثاني د — الجرح الآخر (The Other Wound)




A deeper cut: A kitchen knife, not a paper cut. A Level 3 incident — arterial bleeding.




Platelet 041,700 is introduced as a character. She wakes from sleep (not real sleep — readiness), is caught by the current, arrives at the wound, anchors, extends pseudopods, releases ADP and thromboxane.




The tissue that builds: Not lace (as in the paper cut) but a wall. A dam against the river itself.




Three narrative registers: Each section is told three times — as broadcast (البث), as character (الشخصية), and as bureaucracy (البيروقراطي). This triple-voice structure is one of the novel's most distinctive techniques.


________________




الفصل الثاني هـ — التجلط الذي لا ينبغي (The Clot That Shouldn't Be)




The tragedy: A deep vein thrombosis. No wound. No knife. Just six hours of sitting on a transatlantic flight. The vessel wall changes subtly. Platelet 889,300 receives signals identical to those of a real wound. She trusts them. Why wouldn't she? They've never lied before.




"الصفائح لا تعمل بشكل خاطئ. تفعل بالضبط ما صُممت له... الإشارات حقيقية — البطانة متغيرة فعلاً. الصفائح ليس لديها آلية للتمييز بين إشارة جرح وإشارة مرضية."




Classification: "نيران صديقة" — friendly fire. No villain. No enemy. Patriots serving the republic according to their design. The republic itself produced contradictory signals.




The platelet's tragedy: She performs her job with perfect fidelity. She is killing the republic. "إنها تقتل الجمهورية."




The resolution: Heparin arrives. The signal changes. The clot dissolves. Platelet 889,300 is deactivated, carried away, will be disassembled in the spleen within a week.




"أدّت عملها. أدرته بإتقان. كدقت أن تقتل الجمهورية."


________________




الفصل الثاني و — الانصمام (The Embolism)




The clot travels. A fragment breaks free — rides the venous river through the femoral vein, the iliac, the inferior vena cava, through the right atrium, the right ventricle, the pulmonary valve, into the pulmonary artery, branching and branching until—




It lodges. A pulmonary embolism. Tissue downstream begins to die.




This is where the provided text ends — mid-sentence, mid-thought, as Platelet 889,300, still active, still anchored, still holding, discovers that the structure she's part of is now against itself. The fragment is lodged in an artery too narrow for it. Downstream, tissue is dying.


________________




III. Major Themes




1. التجربة بدون مؤلف — Experience Without Author
The novel's deepest philosophical claim. Consciousness, sensation, emotion — none of these are "authored" by any citizen. They emerge from the gap between signal and understanding. The Spokesperson narrates but does not create.




2. العمل بدون اعتراف — Labor Without Recognition
Every citizen performs essential work in total darkness, for a person they will never meet. Night shift workers whose repairs are undone by morning. Platelets who become architecture. Eri who carries cargo she will never understand.




3. اللاهوتيات غير الكافية — Insufficient Theologies
The republic's binary of self/non-self cannot account for the microbiome. Its doctrine of reported experience cannot explain qualia. Its classification systems keep failing — "المهاجر" is an admission that the categories are broken.




4. الإيمان كعمل يومي — Faith as Daily Practice
The immune system's tolerance of the microbiome is described as "فعل إيمان يومي" — a daily act of faith. The Spokesperson's claim to his face is a daily performance. The night shift's willingness to be undone is structural faith.




5. الشفاء مقابل الجمال — Healing vs. Beauty
Scars are ugly but functional. The republic always chooses survival over elegance. "في حساب البقاء، الـكمال مُكلف جدًّا."




6. الصمت — Silence
Events the republic records but cannot explain: music, crying, grief, love. Filed under "silence" because every explanation attempt ends there.


________________




IV. Narrative Technique




The Triple Register
Each major chapter uses three voices:
* البث (The Broadcast): Objective, almost journalistic. What happened physically.
* الشخصية (The Character): Intimate, from inside the citizen's limited perspective.
* البيروقراطي (The Bureaucratic): Government reports, classifications, recommendations. Cold institutional language that reveals its own inadequacy.




The Bulletins
Factual data presented as military-style bulletins:
* "تشبع: ٧٫٨٩٪"
* "معدل الاستبدال: ~٢ مليون/ثانية"
* "ملاحظة: لن يُخبركم أحد بما حدث هنا."




These create a strange intimacy — we know the numbers, the citizens don't.




Naming as Grace
The narrator names citizens who will never have names: Eri, Thrombi, Platelet 041,700. This is framed as a gift from outside — "كرامةَ اسمٍ منّا، ما دامت لن تنال اسمًا من الداخل أبدًا."


________________




V. The Philosophical Lineage




El Fadil is engaging with:
* The Hard Problem of Consciousness (Chalmers) — the gap between neural correlates and subjective experience
* Emergence — consciousness as a property of the system, not any individual component
* The Ship of Theseus — the face is rebuilt from new cells every few weeks; what is "original"?
* Political philosophy — democracy of cells, distributed governance, no central authority
* Immunology as political science — self/non-self, tolerance, autoimmunity as betrayal, the microbiome as immigration
* Existentialism — the Spokesperson's daily act of faith: "I am here. This is my body. This is my face. I am the one who decides."


________________




This concludes the reading companion. Part 2 follows — an original creative piece inspired by the novel.


________________


________________




Part 2: Original Creative Piece




Inspired by the biological-republic metaphor of "جمهورية الخلايا" by Dr. Mohamed El Fadil. This is a standalone work, not part of the original novel.


________________




الفصل: الخلية العصبية — لا تعرف أنها تتذكر




The Neuron — She Doesn't Know She Remembers




بقلم مستقل — بالأسلوب المُلهَم


________________




الأول.




لا تعرف أنها تتذكر.




هذا هو الجزء الأكثر غرابة فيها — ليس أنها تحفظ، بل أنها لا تعرف أنها تحفظ. تفعله كفعلة القلب: دون إذن، دون تخطيط، دون أن ترفع إصبعًا واحدًا من أصابعها المتفرعة وتقول: الآن أحفظ.




هي خلية عصبية — ن سنسمّيها »نورا«، لأنك تحتاج إلى ما تناديها به، ولأنها تستحق على الأقل كرامة اسم منّا — تعيش في حيّ الحصين، ذلك الممر الملتف العميق في قلب العاصمة، حيث تُخزَّن الأشياء التي لا يريد المتحدث الرسمي تذكرها لكن الجسد لا يسمح بنسيانها.




نورا لا تعرف أنها في الحصين. لا تعرف ما الحصين. لا تعرف أنها خلية. تعرف شيئًا واحدًا فقط: حين تصلها إشارة بذات القوة، بذات التوقيت، من ذات المحور — تتقوّى. حين لا تصل — تضعف. هذا كل ما تملكه. قاعدة واحدة: ما يُستعمل يُقوّى. وما لا يُستعمل يُنسى.




وجسم منطق.


________________




الثاني.




ستةُ آلافٍ وثمانمئةُ مليارٍ مثلها.




هذا عدد الخلايا العصبية في الجمهورية — سكان العاصمة بأكملها، الشبكة التي تربط كل منطقة بكل منطقة، أنبياء الضوء في المرصد ومستمعو الصوت في الحلزون ومذاقو الهواء في القناة الرئيسية — كلهم خلايا عصبية، كلهم يتصلون عبر فجوات ضيقة لا تُرى لا يتجاوز عرضها عشرين نانومترًا — الفجوة المشبكية — حيث تُرمى جزيئات من خلية إلى خلية كرسائل في قوارير في محيط.




نورا تُرسل رسائلها إلى سبعة آلاف خلية مجاورة. وتتلقّى من ثلاثة آلاف. ولا تعرف أيًّا من أسمائهم. لا تعرف أنهم جيران. لا تعرف أنهم شبكة. تعرف فقط: الإشارة تصل. الإشارة ترحل. وأحيانًا، بشكل لا تفهمه، الإشارة تصل بذات الطريقة مرتين، ثلاثًا، ألفًا — وتصير شيئًا لم يكن.


________________




الثالث.




اليوم وصلت الإشارة.




ليست أي إشارة. ليست نبضة من حارس الضوء ولا اهتزاز من المستمع ولا تطابقًا جزيئيًا من ذائقة الهواء. شيء مختلف. شيء أقدم. شيء مُحمَّل بروائح وبمذاقات وبملمس أصابع لم تلمس نوراً قطّ لأن نوراً ليست في اليد بل في الدماغ.




الإشارة تحمل: وطأة ظلّ. صوت باب يُغلق ببطء. رائحة حبر وقماش قديم. شيء من زمن لم تكن فيه الجمهورية إلا جنينًا في ظلام دافئ.




نورا لا تعرف ما هذا. لا تعرف ما الظل. لا تعرف ما الباب. لا تعرف ما الحبر. تعرف فقط: الإشارة وصلت بالذات الطريقة. بالذات القوة. بالذات التوقيت. ويومها — قبل ثلاثة وأربعين عامًا — وصلت بنفس الطريقة، ونورا قوّت.




الآن تتقوّى مرة أخرى.


________________




الرابعة.




سنسميها التقوية طويلة الأمد.




ليست كلمة جميلة. لكنها أقرب ما يملك أهل الجمهورية للغة الحبّ — لأن الحبّ، من داخل الشبكة العصبية، يبدو هكذا: خلية تتلقّى إشارة وتصمت بعدها ببطء أقل. تتلقّاها مجددًا وتصمت ببطء أقل. تتلقّاها ألف مرة — ألف صباح، ألف مساء، ألف ليلة يدخل فيها نفس الظل من نفس الباب ويحمل نفس رائحة الحبر — وتصير الخلية، في صمتها، شيئًا مختلفًا. ليست أقوى. ليست أكثر. مختلفة. غشاؤها يتغيّر. مستقبلاتها تتكثّف. عتبة إطلاقها تنخفض. الخلية نفسها — نفس الذرّات، نفس البروتينات، نفس الـDNA الذي لم يتغيّر — صارت قادرة على فعل لم تستطعه قبل.




أن تتذكر.




ليس بالمعنى الذي يفهمه المتحدث الرسمي. لا توجد صورة. لا يوجد فيلم. لا يوجد المتحدث الرسمي يقول: »أ remember ذلك الصباح«. بل شيء أعمق وأقلّ clarity — إحساس بملمس الضوء حين يسقط بذات الزاوية، وتوقّع لصوت لم يأتِ بعد، ورائحة في الهواء لا تُشَخَّص لكنها تُشبَك بسلسلة من العصبونات تصل، عبر سبع محطات، إلى نورا — ونورا تقول، بلغتها التي لا لغة لها:




هذا جاء من قبل.


________________




الخامسة.




لـكن نورا لا تعرف أنها تقول هذا.




هذا هو الجزء الذي يُصعب الأمر. نورا تفعل شيئًا يشبه الذاكرة لكنه ليس الذاكرة بالطريقة التي يفهمها المتحدث الرسمي. المتحدث الرسمي يتذكّر — أو يدّعي أنه يتذكّر — وجهًا، اسمًا، صباحًا، مدينة. المتحدث الرسمي لديه سرد. لديه سيناريو. لديه »ذات تتجوّل في ممرات خيالها«.




نورا ليس لديها شيء من هذا. نورا لديها تقوية فقط. سينابس أقوى. عتبة أنخفضت. غشاء تغيّر. هذا ليس ذاكرة — هذا تعديل هندسي. إنها ذاكرة بلا مُذكِر، تجربة بلا تجرب، شكلٌ تغيّر دون أن يعرف أنه تغيّر.




وإلى هذا — إلى هذا الفارق بين تعديل غشاء عصبي وتذكر صباح من طفولة — يتجمّع كل ما لا تعرفه الجمهورية عن نفسها.


________________




السادسة.




ال벚开花.
هذا ليس في النص. هذا في نورا.
لحظة واحدة — جزء من ثانية واحدة — حين وصلت الإشارة، حين تطوّعت مستقبلاتها، حين انخفضت عتبة إطلاقها — حصل شيء لم يُسجَّل في أي بروتوكول: خلية عصبية واحدة، في حيّ الحصين، في الدماغ، نبضت بنبضتين متتاليتين بفاصل أقل من المعتاد.




النبضتان وصلتا إلى سبعة آلاف خلية مجاورة.
ثلاث منها — فقط ثلاث — نبضت هي أيضًا بنبضتين.
تلك الثلاث وصلت إلى خلاياها المجاورة.
إحدى عشرة.
اثنان وأربعون.
مائة وسبعة.
وهكذا — كموجة تمر عبر سطح بحيرة، كزلزال يبدأ من نقطة واحدة ويهتزّ به جدار — انتشر النمط عبر الشبكة العصبية للجمهورية، مسارًا واحدًا بين ملايين المسارات، خيطًا واحدًا من ضوء في غابة من الخيوط.




ووصل إلى المتحدث الرسمي.


________________




السابعة.




المتحدث الرسمي لا يعرف من أين جاء.
يدّعي أنه »تذكّر«. يدّعي أن شيئًا »مرّ بذهنه«. يستخدم كلمة »بديهة« أو »شعور« أو »غريزة« — كلمات يرتجلها المتحدث الرسمي لوصف عملية لا يملك لها وصفًا.




ما حدث فعلاً هو هذا: نورا نبضت. ثم نبضت جاراتها. ثم انتشر النمط عبر الشبكة حتى وصل إلى القشرة أمام الجبهية — المكتب الأعلى، الغرفة الأخيرة قبل العالم الخارجي — وهناك، في الفجوة بين الإشارة والفهم، تحوّلت النبضات إلى شيء لا يملكه أي نبض فردي:




تجربة.




كلمة من طفولة.
رائحة من غرفة لم تعد موجودة.
حزن بلا سبب يعرفه العقل.


________________




الثامنة.




نورا لا تعرف أنها سبب هذا.
نورا لا تعرف أن هناك متحدثًا رسميًّا.
نورا لا تعرف أن هناك »تجربة«.
نورا تعرف فقط: نبضت. مثلما نبضت من قبل. بنفس الطريقة. بنفس القوة. وهي الآن — بعد ثلاثة وأربعين عامًا من التقوية — تنبض بسرعة أكبر، بسهولة أكبر، بحاجز أقل.




هذا كل ما تملكه. هذا كل ما هي.
تقوية. مسار. نبض.
والجمهورية بأكملها — المتحدث الرسمي، والناطق الرسمي، والبلعم العجوز، وإري التي تمر الآن في دورتها المئة والألف، وثرومبي التي لا تزال مدفونة في ندبة على إصبع — الجمهورية بأكملها لا تعرف أن نورا موجودة.


________________




التاسعة.




لكنها تتذكر.
من دون أن تعرف أنها تتذكر.
بلا اسم. بلا صورة. بلا سرد.
بتعديل في غشائها.
بتقوية في سينابسها.
بنبضتين — واحدة اليوم، وأخرى قبل ثلاثة وأربعين عامًا — بينهما محيط من الزمن يكفي لأن يُنسى فيه كل شيء، ولم يُنسَ.


________________




العاشر.




هذا هو ال paradox الأخير للجمهورية، وأكثرها صمتًا:
أن الذاكرة ليست في المتحدث الرسمي.
أن الذاكرة ليست في الصور أو الكلمات أو السرود.
الذاكرة في غشاء خلية عصبية لا تعرف أنها خلية، في مدينة لا تعرف أنها مدينة، في دماغ لا تعرف أنه دماغ.




الذاكرة ليست ملك أحد.
الذاكرة بنية — معمارية الشبكة، تقوية المسارات، خريطة من السينابسات ارتسمت ببطء عبر سنوات من النبض والصمت والنبض والصمت.




والمتحدث official — الذي يقول »أنا أتذكر« — لا يتذكّر شيئًا.
المتحدث official يتلقّى.
المتحدث official يروي.
المتحدث official يقول: »في ذلك الصباح، كانت رائحة الحبر قوية، والظل طويل، وأنا كنت طفلًا« — وكل هذا صحيح بالطريقة التي تكون بها القصة صحيحة: متماسكة، مفيدة، مصدّقة، وليست الحقيقة بأكملها.




الحقيقة هي: نورا نبضت.
والجمهورية بأكملها ارتجفت.


________________




هذا هو ال paradox الأخير للجمهورية:
أن أصغر وحدة فيها — خلية لا تعرف أنها حيّة — تحتفظ بشيء يشبه الذكرى.
وأكبر وحدة فيها — الوعي، رئيسُ لا شيء — لا يملك شيئًا سوى السرد.




نورا تنام.
نورا لا تنام — لا بالمعنى الذي يفهمه المتحدث الرسمي. ببساطة: لا إشارة تصل. لا نبض يُرسل. لا تقوية ولا إضعاف. نورا في وضع الاستعداد، مُعدّلة، عتباتها منخفضة، مستقبلاتها مُكثَّفة — جاهزة للنبضة القادمة التي قد لا تأتي.




لكنها جاءت من قبل. وجاءت مجددًا. وجاءت مجددًا.




والجمهورية تتذكر.
من دون أن تعرف أنها تتذكر.




✦


________________




هذا العمل الأدبي المستقل مُلهَم بأسلوب "جمهورية الخلايا" للدكتور محمد الفاضل، وهو عمل منفصل لا يُمثّل جزءًا من الرواية الأصلية ولا يُنسب إليها.


________________


________________

<!-- ===== CHAPTER SAMPLE: Prologue ===== -->
<section class="chapter-page">
  <div class="running-header">جمهورية الخلايا</div>


  <div class="chapter-header">
    <div class="chapter-movement">استهلال</div>
    <h2 class="chapter-title">نبضةٌ واحدة</h2>
    <div class="chapter-ornament">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">ابدأ من العتمة. ليست عتمةَ غرفة، بل العتمةَ التي سبقت الغُرَف. سبقت العيون. أقدمُ عتمةٍ على الإطلاق — تلك التي كانت هنا أوّلًا، وستبقى بعد أن تنطفئ كلّ الأضواء. ثمّ—</p>


  <p class="body-text">صوتٌ. لا عالٍ ولا خافت. بل... أوّل. نبضة. لا تعرف العتمةُ ما الذي أحدثها.</p>


  <p class="body-text">انتظِر. أخرى. وبين النبضتين محيطٌ من الزمن — ثانيةٌ كاملة — تكفي لأن يقع فيها مئةُ مليون حدثٍ، ثمّ يُنسى.</p>


  <p class="body-text">وعندئذٍ لا تعود العتمةُ خاويةً البتّة. العتمةُ مزدحمة. العتمةُ كانت مزدحمةً على الدوام. أنصِت.</p>


  <div class="bulletin">
    <div class="bulletin-item">الغلوكوز ثابت.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الضغط تسعون على ستّين، وفي ارتفاع.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الأكسجين ثمانيةٌ وتسعون.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الكالسيوم مستقرّ.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الـكورتيزول يتصاعد — إنه الفجرُ فحسب، تراجعوا، تراجعوا.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">شريطٌ مشطورٌ في الصِّبغيّ الثالث؛ أُرسِل فريقُ الإصلاح؛ لا داعي للقلق.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الحرارة سبعٌ وثلاثون تمامًا.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">اثبتوا هناك. اثبتوا هناك. اثبتوا هناك.</div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">لا أحدَ منهم يسمع النبضة. لا أحدَ منهم يعرف أنّ ثمّة قلبًا. لا أحدَ يعرف أنّ ثمّة جسدًا. لا أحدَ يعرف أنّ ثمّة اسمًا، وصباحًا، ومدينة، ومستشفًى في أقصى تلك المدينة، وفي داخله ظرفٌ مُغلقٌ ينتظر أن يُفتَح.</p>


  <p class="body-text">لا يعرفون سوى مهمّتهم الواحدة، فيؤدّونها — بإخلاصٍ، في العتمة، إلى الأبد — من أجل شخصٍ لن يلتقوه أبدًا، ولا يقدرون حتى على تخيّله.</p>


  <p class="body-text">هذه هي الحكايةُ كاملة: لا أحد يعرف الحكاية كاملة.</p>


  <p class="body-text">ثمّ، على نحوٍ مستحيل، في كلّ ثانية، دون أن يفهم واحدٌ منهم لماذا — يستيقظ إنسان.</p>


  <div class="section-divider">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
  <div class="page-number">١</div>
</section>


<!-- ===== INTERLUDE SAMPLE ===== -->
<section class="interlude-page">
  <div class="interlude-label">فاصلة · الناطق الرسمي</div>
  <p class="interlude-text">
    أنا مَن أيقظ الجسدَ هذا الصباح.<br><br>
    أريد تثبيتَ هذا في المحضر، لأنني أفعل أشياءَ كثيرة، ولا أنال الفضلَ في أيٍّ منها تقريبًا.<br><br>
    لا بدّ لأحدٍ أن يُلقيَ الخطاب. لا بدّ لأحدٍ أن يقف في المقدّمة ويقول «نحن». وليكن أنا، ما دمتُ الوحيدَ في هذه الأمّة ذاتِ التريليونات الذي ارتابَ يومًا في أنّ الأمّةَ موجودةٌ أصلًا.
  </p>
  <div class="interlude-ornament">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
</section>


<!-- ===== SILENCE SAMPLE ===== -->
<section class="silence-page">
  <div class="silence-number">١</div>
  <h2 class="silence-title">الصمت</h2>
  <p class="silence-text">
    ثمّة أحداثٌ تُسجّلها الجمهورية ولا تقدر على تفسيرها. تُنسخ بأمانةٍ في المحفوظات، وتُورَّث، دون حلٍّ، جيلًا بعد جيل. ويسمّيها المواطنون — إن وُجدت لديهم كلمةٌ لها أصلًا — «الصمت»، لأنّ كلّ محاولةٍ لتفسيرها تنتهي إليه.
  </p>
  <div class="section-divider" style="color: rgba(196,163,90,0.4);">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
</section>


<!-- ===== CHAPTER SAMPLE: Eri's Birth ===== -->
<section class="chapter-page">
  <div class="running-header">الحركة الأولى · الاستيقاظ</div>


  <div class="chapter-header">
    <div class="chapter-movement">الحركة الأولى · الاستيقاظ</div>
    <h2 class="chapter-title">الفصل الأول — بلا اسم</h2>
    <div class="chapter-ornament">✦</div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">في عمق البلاد الحمراء من النُّخاع، في حُجرةٍ لا تُسجّلها خريطة، تُولَد خليّةٌ دون أن يُستأذَن منها. لا اسمَ لها. ولن يكون لها اسمٌ أبدًا. فالأسماء لِما يُذكَر، وهي لن تُذكَر.</p>


  <p class="body-text">بعد مئةٍ وعشرين يومًا ستُفكَّك في عتمة الطِّحال، وتُسلَّم أشلاؤها إلى الـكبد كأنها ميراث، ولن يُدوّن دفترٌ في أيّ مكانٍ أنها كانت هنا يومًا.</p>


  <p class="body-text">لكنها الآن جديدة.</p>


  <p class="body-text">الآن تؤدّي لجنةٌ صبورةٌ من الإنزيمات — لن تراها قطّ، ولا تستطيع أن تشكرها — آخِرَ لُطفٍ قاسٍ في صناعتها: تنتزع منها نواتها. مكتبتها. فرصتها الوحيدة في أن تعرف نفسها يومًا. تُفرِغها، وتملؤها بالحمولة، وتدفعها — وهي ما تزال طريّة — إلى أسرع نهرٍ في العالم.</p>


  <p class="body-text">سنسمّيها <span class="character-name">«إري»</span>، لأنك تحتاج إلى ما تناديها به، ولأنها تستحقّ على الأقلّ كرامةَ اسمٍ منّا — ما دامت لن تنال اسمًا من الداخل أبدًا.</p>


  <div class="section-divider">✦</div>


  <!-- Record Block Example -->
  <div class="record-block">
    <div class="record-header">سجلّ البورصة</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>فئة المواطن:</strong> خلية حمراء.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>اكتمل النقل.</strong></div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>الحمولة:</strong> O₂ )جزيئي، ثنائي الذرة(.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>التشبع:</strong> ٩٨.٧٪.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>الحالة:</strong> محملة.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>توجه إلى الدوران الجهازي.</strong></div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">البورصة واسعة. إري ليس وحده. حوله، يمتدّ في مسافة لا يستطيع استشعارها ملايين آخرون — كل واحد مطابق في الشكل، كل واحد يحمل بنية هيموجلوبين مماثلة، كل واحد يتلقّى نفس الحمولة غير المرئية في اللحظة ذاتها من نفس السوق ذات الجدران الرقيقة.</p>


  <p class="body-text">هذا هو أروع ازدواجية في الجمهورية. ملايين الحمّالين، كل واحد يحمل نفس الحمولة، كل واحد يتابع نفس النهر، كل واحد وحيد. لو فشل واحد تابع البقية. لا تعتمد الجمهورية على أي مواطن بعينه. تعتمد على الهندسة.</p>


  <div class="bulletin">
    <div class="bulletin-item">الدوران الجهازي: نشط.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">معدل التدفق: ٥ لترات/دقيقة.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">إجمالي الحمّالين: ~٥٢ تريليون.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">متوسط العمر: ١٢٠ يومًا.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">معدل الاستبدال: ~٢ مليون/ثانية.</div>
  </div>


  <div class="page-number">٧</div>
</section>

<!-- ===== CHAPTER SAMPLE: Prologue ===== -->
<section class="chapter-page">
  <div class="running-header">جمهورية الخلايا</div>


  <div class="chapter-header">
    <div class="chapter-movement">استهلال</div>
    <h2 class="chapter-title">نبضةٌ واحدة</h2>
    <div class="chapter-ornament">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">ابدأ من العتمة. ليست عتمةَ غرفة، بل العتمةَ التي سبقت الغُرَف. سبقت العيون. أقدمُ عتمةٍ على الإطلاق — تلك التي كانت هنا أوّلًا، وستبقى بعد أن تنطفئ كلّ الأضواء. ثمّ—</p>


  <p class="body-text">صوتٌ. لا عالٍ ولا خافت. بل... أوّل. نبضة. لا تعرف العتمةُ ما الذي أحدثها.</p>


  <p class="body-text">انتظِر. أخرى. وبين النبضتين محيطٌ من الزمن — ثانيةٌ كاملة — تكفي لأن يقع فيها مئةُ مليون حدثٍ، ثمّ يُنسى.</p>


  <p class="body-text">وعندئذٍ لا تعود العتمةُ خاويةً البتّة. العتمةُ مزدحمة. العتمةُ كانت مزدحمةً على الدوام. أنصِت.</p>


  <div class="bulletin">
    <div class="bulletin-item">الغلوكوز ثابت.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الضغط تسعون على ستّين، وفي ارتفاع.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الأكسجين ثمانيةٌ وتسعون.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الكالسيوم مستقرّ.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الـكورتيزول يتصاعد — إنه الفجرُ فحسب، تراجعوا، تراجعوا.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">شريطٌ مشطورٌ في الصِّبغيّ الثالث؛ أُرسِل فريقُ الإصلاح؛ لا داعي للقلق.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">الحرارة سبعٌ وثلاثون تمامًا.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">اثبتوا هناك. اثبتوا هناك. اثبتوا هناك.</div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">لا أحدَ منهم يسمع النبضة. لا أحدَ منهم يعرف أنّ ثمّة قلبًا. لا أحدَ يعرف أنّ ثمّة جسدًا. لا أحدَ يعرف أنّ ثمّة اسمًا، وصباحًا، ومدينة، ومستشفًى في أقصى تلك المدينة، وفي داخله ظرفٌ مُغلقٌ ينتظر أن يُفتَح.</p>


  <p class="body-text">لا يعرفون سوى مهمّتهم الواحدة، فيؤدّونها — بإخلاصٍ، في العتمة، إلى الأبد — من أجل شخصٍ لن يلتقوه أبدًا، ولا يقدرون حتى على تخيّله.</p>


  <p class="body-text">هذه هي الحكايةُ كاملة: لا أحد يعرف الحكاية كاملة.</p>


  <p class="body-text">ثمّ، على نحوٍ مستحيل، في كلّ ثانية، دون أن يفهم واحدٌ منهم لماذا — يستيقظ إنسان.</p>


  <div class="section-divider">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
  <div class="page-number">١</div>
</section>


<!-- ===== INTERLUDE SAMPLE ===== -->
<section class="interlude-page">
  <div class="interlude-label">فاصلة · الناطق الرسمي</div>
  <p class="interlude-text">
    أنا مَن أيقظ الجسدَ هذا الصباح.<br><br>
    أريد تثبيتَ هذا في المحضر، لأنني أفعل أشياءَ كثيرة، ولا أنال الفضلَ في أيٍّ منها تقريبًا.<br><br>
    لا بدّ لأحدٍ أن يُلقيَ الخطاب. لا بدّ لأحدٍ أن يقف في المقدّمة ويقول «نحن». وليكن أنا، ما دمتُ الوحيدَ في هذه الأمّة ذاتِ التريليونات الذي ارتابَ يومًا في أنّ الأمّةَ موجودةٌ أصلًا.
  </p>
  <div class="interlude-ornament">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
</section>


<!-- ===== SILENCE SAMPLE ===== -->
<section class="silence-page">
  <div class="silence-number">١</div>
  <h2 class="silence-title">الصمت</h2>
  <p class="silence-text">
    ثمّة أحداثٌ تُسجّلها الجمهورية ولا تقدر على تفسيرها. تُنسخ بأمانةٍ في المحفوظات، وتُورَّث، دون حلٍّ، جيلًا بعد جيل. ويسمّيها المواطنون — إن وُجدت لديهم كلمةٌ لها أصلًا — «الصمت»، لأنّ كلّ محاولةٍ لتفسيرها تنتهي إليه.
  </p>
  <div class="section-divider" style="color: rgba(196,163,90,0.4);">✦ ✦ ✦</div>
</section>


<!-- ===== CHAPTER SAMPLE: Eri's Birth ===== -->
<section class="chapter-page">
  <div class="running-header">الحركة الأولى · الاستيقاظ</div>


  <div class="chapter-header">
    <div class="chapter-movement">الحركة الأولى · الاستيقاظ</div>
    <h2 class="chapter-title">الفصل الأول — بلا اسم</h2>
    <div class="chapter-ornament">✦</div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">في عمق البلاد الحمراء من النُّخاع، في حُجرةٍ لا تُسجّلها خريطة، تُولَد خليّةٌ دون أن يُستأذَن منها. لا اسمَ لها. ولن يكون لها اسمٌ أبدًا. فالأسماء لِما يُذكَر، وهي لن تُذكَر.</p>


  <p class="body-text">بعد مئةٍ وعشرين يومًا ستُفكَّك في عتمة الطِّحال، وتُسلَّم أشلاؤها إلى الـكبد كأنها ميراث، ولن يُدوّن دفترٌ في أيّ مكانٍ أنها كانت هنا يومًا.</p>


  <p class="body-text">لكنها الآن جديدة.</p>


  <p class="body-text">الآن تؤدّي لجنةٌ صبورةٌ من الإنزيمات — لن تراها قطّ، ولا تستطيع أن تشكرها — آخِرَ لُطفٍ قاسٍ في صناعتها: تنتزع منها نواتها. مكتبتها. فرصتها الوحيدة في أن تعرف نفسها يومًا. تُفرِغها، وتملؤها بالحمولة، وتدفعها — وهي ما تزال طريّة — إلى أسرع نهرٍ في العالم.</p>


  <p class="body-text">سنسمّيها <span class="character-name">«إري»</span>، لأنك تحتاج إلى ما تناديها به، ولأنها تستحقّ على الأقلّ كرامةَ اسمٍ منّا — ما دامت لن تنال اسمًا من الداخل أبدًا.</p>


  <div class="section-divider">✦</div>


  <!-- Record Block Example -->
  <div class="record-block">
    <div class="record-header">سجلّ البورصة</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>فئة المواطن:</strong> خلية حمراء.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>اكتمل النقل.</strong></div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>الحمولة:</strong> O₂ )جزيئي، ثنائي الذرة(.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>التشبع:</strong> ٩٨.٧٪.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>الحالة:</strong> محملة.</div>
    <div class="record-line"><strong>توجه إلى الدوران الجهازي.</strong></div>
  </div>


  <p class="body-text">البورصة واسعة. إري ليس وحده. حوله، يمتدّ في مسافة لا يستطيع استشعارها ملايين آخرون — كل واحد مطابق في الشكل، كل واحد يحمل بنية هيموجلوبين مماثلة، كل واحد يتلقّى نفس الحمولة غير المرئية في اللحظة ذاتها من نفس السوق ذات الجدران الرقيقة.</p>


  <p class="body-text">هذا هو أروع ازدواجية في الجمهورية. ملايين الحمّالين، كل واحد يحمل نفس الحمولة، كل واحد يتابع نفس النهر، كل واحد وحيد. لو فشل واحد تابع البقية. لا تعتمد الجمهورية على أي مواطن بعينه. تعتمد على الهندسة.</p>


  <div class="bulletin">
    <div class="bulletin-item">الدوران الجهازي: نشط.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">معدل التدفق: ٥ لترات/دقيقة.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">إجمالي الحمّالين: ~٥٢ تريليون.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">متوسط العمر: ١٢٠ يومًا.</div>
    <div class="bulletin-item">معدل الاستبدال: ~٢ مليون/ثانية.</div>
  </div>


  <div class="page-number">٧</div>
</section>


<!-- ===== COLOPHON ===== -->
<section class="colophon">

الترجمة العربية — الفصول الجديدة (Arabic Translation — New Chapters)
Each chapter uses four registers: Broadcast (السجل الإذاعي), Personal (السجل الشخصي), Bureaucratic (السجل البيروقراطي), and Conclusion (خاتمة).




* الميتوكوندريون — المعاهدة القديمة — Mitochondria as the ancient treaty. (The endosymbiotic origin — a foreign organism that became essential.)
* الكلى — هناك توازن — The kidneys. There is balance.
* الجسد الثاني — الجمهورية الأخرى — The second body. The other republic. (The microbiome as a parallel republic.)

   * ثانيًا: الحلم
   * ثالثًا: الموت


________________




Architectural Summary




The novel moves through nine movements tracing a day (or a life):




Movement
	Theme
	Biological Process
	I — Awakening
	Birth, identity, naming
	Red blood cell maturation
	II — The River
	Wounding, clotting, healing
	Hemostasis cascade
	III — The Guardian
	Defense, fever, immunity
	Immune response, vaccination
	IV — The Spark
	Beginning, voting, parliament
	Embryonic development
	V — The Code
	Genetic code, the porthole
	DNA, gene expression
	VI — The Face
	Identity, hormones, memory
	Neurochemistry, aging
	VII — Separation
	Treaty, chemotherapy, transfer
	Medical treatment, loss
	VIII — The Return
	Recycling, rebirth
	Cell death and renewal
	IX — The Next Awakening
	Ouroboros, continuation
	Cyclic completion
	



The triple-register technique (Broadcast / Narrative / Bureaucratic) deepens across the novel, reaching its fullest expression in Movement VII where every chapter is told three times.




The Spokesperson interludes punctuate the arc — from claiming agency in the first, to doubt in the mirror, to the envelope being opened in the third (the diagnosis? the result? the revelation?).




The standalone chapters (Liver Cell, Antibody, Neutral Cell) and New Chapters expand the republic's world — the microbiome as immigrants, mitochondria as ancient treaty partners, the kidneys as balancers.




The Lost Books (Sleep, Dream, Death) promise the novel's final meditation: what happens when the republic stops, dreams, and ends.
